  <row Id="132835353" PostId="75272906" Score="0" Text="please do not use `thread::sleep` instead of a proper solution like join handles or other concurrency structures to wait for a thread to finish. This introduces race conditions because we can never guarantee if the thread will exit by the time the sleep finishes. The OS scheduler may start the thread immediately on another core in your machine, but odds are it will need to wait for a time slot to become available. Your machine likely has hundreds or thousands of threads running at a given time across different applications and they are all waiting for CPU time."   <row Id="135376472" PostId="76789433" Score="0" Text="If you know that B follows A in memory, then `reinterpret_cast&lt;uintptr_t&gt;(a-&gt;ptr) - reinterpret_cast&lt;uintptr_t&gt;(a);` is a *constant* (`sizeof(A)`) so it doesn't make sense to serialize it at all (or have it in the first place). If you don't know that, then `reinterpret_cast&lt;uintptr_t&gt;(a-&gt;ptr) - reinterpret_cast&lt;uintptr_t&gt;(a);` is just a meaningless number that won't help you in any way. There are ways to serialize linked data structures but this ain't one." CreationDate="2023-07-28T17:25:05.770" UserId="775806" ContentLicense="CC BY-SA 4.0" />

  <row Id="135792894" PostId="77019939" Score="1" Text="The directory path assigned to the environment variable `HOMEPATH` begins always with a backslash. There should not be used `c:\%HOMEPATH%` as that results finally after environment variable expansion in `c:\\Users\User.Name` which the Windows file IO functions must later automatically correct most likely multiple times to `c:\Users\User.Name`. It would be better to use `%HOMEDRIVE%%HOMEPATH%` instead of `C:\%HOMEPATH%` or much better `%USERPROFILE%` and `%LOCALAPPDATA%` instead of `C:\%HOMEPATH%\AppData\Local` in the batch script."   <row Id="136883585" PostId="77644012" Score="0" Text="By doing ```5000 * index```, you're effectively adding a delay to each ```setTimeout``` call. The first item will have a delay of 0 seconds, the second item will have a delay of 5 seconds, the third item will have a delay of 10 seconds, and so on. This ensures that each ```setTimeout``` is delayed by a different amount of time, so the ```Date``` is updated for each file. Without this, all the ```setTimeout``` calls would be delayed by the same amount of time, and they would all use the same initial timestamp." CreationDate="2023-12-12T06:24:50.773" UserId="21370707" ContentLicense="CC BY-SA 4.0" />

  <row Id="136931932" PostId="77617164" Score="0" Text="Another way to think of it: An awk script is made up of `condition { action }` statements. If you  write `awk 'foo'` with no explicit action then that's equivalent to writing `foo { print }` and the default action, `print`, is executed if `foo` evaluates to true. So, if `print` is the `action` then what is `foo`? It's a condition as that's the only other possibility and it's being tested for a true/false result as conditions always are."
